###begin article-title 0
###xml 0 6 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Murine</span>
Murine Dishevelled 3 Functions in Redundant Pathways with Dishevelled 1 and 2 in Normal Cardiac Outflow Tract, Cochlea, and Neural Tube Development
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Current address: Burnham Institute for Medical Research, La Jolla, California, United States of America
###end p 1
###begin p 2
Current address: Department of Medicine, Eastern Virginia Medical School, Norfolk, Virginia, United States of America
###end p 2
###begin p 3
Current address: Department of Cell Biology, School of Medicine, University of Alabama, Birmingham, Alabama, United States of America
###end p 3
###begin p 4

###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 387 390 384 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 449 453 446 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 458 462 455 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 526 530 523 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 615 625 612 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvls. Dvl3</italic>
###xml 625 628 622 625 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 943 954 940 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2/Ltap</italic>
###xml 956 962 953 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 1012 1016 1009 1013 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1016 1019 1013 1016 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1024 1030 1021 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 1042 1046 1039 1043 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1046 1049 1043 1046 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1050 1056 1047 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 1165 1169 1162 1166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1189 1193 1186 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 1198 1202 1195 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 1244 1248 1241 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1288 1291 1285 1288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1308 1311 1305 1308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1336 1339 1333 1336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1379 1383 1376 1380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvls</italic>
###xml 1531 1534 1528 1531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1564 1567 1561 1564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1660 1664 1657 1661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1879 1883 1876 1880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvls</italic>
###xml 608 614 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 629 633 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Dishevelled (Dvl) proteins are important signaling components of both the canonical beta-catenin/Wnt pathway, which controls cell proliferation and patterning, and the planar cell polarity (PCP) pathway, which coordinates cell polarity within a sheet of cells and also directs convergent extension cell (CE) movements that produce narrowing and elongation of the tissue. Three mammalian Dvl genes have been identified and the developmental roles of Dvl1 and Dvl2 were previously determined. Here, we identify the functions of Dvl3 in development and provide evidence of functional redundancy among the three murine Dvls. Dvl3-/- mice died perinatally with cardiac outflow tract abnormalities, including double outlet right ventricle and persistent truncus arteriosis. These mutants also displayed a misorientated stereocilia in the organ of Corti, a phenotype that was enhanced with the additional loss of a single allele of the PCP component Vangl2/Ltap (LtapLp/+). Although neurulation appeared normal in both Dvl3-/- and LtapLp/+ mutants, Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ combined mutants displayed incomplete neural tube closure. Importantly, we show that many of the roles of Dvl3 are also shared by Dvl1 and Dvl2. More severe phenotypes were observed in Dvl3 mutants with the deficiency of another Dvl, and increasing Dvl dosage genetically with Dvl transgenes demonstrated the ability of Dvls to compensate for each other to enable normal development. Interestingly, global canonical Wnt signaling appeared largely unaffected in the double Dvl mutants, suggesting that low Dvl levels are sufficient for functional canonical Wnt signals. In summary, we demonstrate that Dvl3 is required for cardiac outflow tract development and describe its importance in the PCP pathway during neurulation and cochlea development. Finally, we establish several developmental processes in which the three Dvls are functionally redundant.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Author Summary
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 321 332 321 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dishevelled</italic>
###xml 334 337 334 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 386 390 386 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 499 503 499 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 692 695 692 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 964 967 964 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 1029 1032 1029 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 507 511 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 656 660 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 829 834 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 951 955 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1061 1067 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
Multi-gene families, comprising a set of very similar genes with shared nucleotide sequences, are common in mammals. Individual family members may be expressed in different places and perform separate functions. Alternatively, the genes may have redundant functions, but distinct dosage requirements. Mammals share three Dishevelled (Dvl) family members and while the roles of Dvl1 and Dvl2 have been described previously, the functions of Dvl3 have remained elusive. Here, we show that the lack of Dvl3 in mice affects the formation of the heart, neural tube, and inner ear. We further show that the defects in these tissues are much more severe when the mice are deficient in more than one Dvl family member, indicating redundant functions for these genes. Congenital heart disease affects approximately 75 in every 1,000 live human births, and approximately 30% of these diseases are due to disruptions in the outflow tract, the region affected in mice lacking Dvl genes. Neural tube defects, similar to those observed in the Dvl mutants, are also common in humans. The animal models described here provide useful tools to elucidate the genetic mechanisms that underlie these abnormalities and may provide novel ways of treating these disorders in the future.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
Introduction
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 461 464 461 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Huelsken1">[1]</xref>
###xml 465 468 465 468 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Yamaguchi1">[2]</xref>
###xml 838 841 838 841 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Curtin1">[3]</xref>
###xml 842 845 842 845 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Zallen1">[7]</xref>
Normal mammalian development is the result of complex signaling networks that regulate and coordinate cell behavior. Wnt signaling controls a broad spectrum of cell fate decisions during embryogenesis and is critical for cell to cell communication in mammalian development. Through the activation of specific target genes, the canonical Wnt pathway tightly regulates cell proliferation, differentiation, adhesion and survival, and controls embryonic patterning [1],[2]. A non-canonical Wnt planar cell polarity (PCP) pathway, parallel to that first discovered in flies, has been described in mammals, where it regulates cell polarity and convergent extension (CE) movements. In these coordinated cell movements, cells migrate medially and intercalate, producing an elongation and narrowing of the tissue along the anterior-posterior axis [3]-[7].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 83 86 83 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Klingensmith1">[8]</xref>
###xml 87 91 87 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Yang1">[13]</xref>
###xml 313 317 313 317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Malbon1">[14]</xref>
###xml 318 322 318 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wallingford1">[15]</xref>
###xml 67 73 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 78 82 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Dishevelled (Dvl) proteins, of which three have been identified in humans and mice [8]-[13] are highly conserved components of both the canonical Wnt and PCP signaling cascades. They function as essential scaffold proteins that interact with diverse proteins, including kinases, phosphatases and adaptor proteins [14],[15]. In the canonical Wnt pathway, Dvl transduces the signal activated by Wnt binding to membrane-bound Frizzled (Fz) receptors and low-density lipoprotein-related receptor protein (LRP) 5/6 co-receptors, causing the stabilization and cytosolic accumulation of the critical mediator, beta-catenin. Following the translocation of beta-catenin to the nucleus, it then binds with members of the T-cell factor (TCF)/lymphocyte enhancer factor (Lef) family of transcription factors to regulate the expression of target genes. Dvl is also one of the core components of the PCP signaling pathway, in addition to Fz, Van Gogh/Strabismus (Vang/Stbm), Flamingo/Starry night (Fmi/Stan), Diego (Dgo) and Prickle (Pk). The specific, highly controlled, asymmetric arrangement of these proteins allows polarity of the cell to be established within the plane of the epithelium and promotes the rearrangement of the cytoskeletal components of the cell.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 163 167 163 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Buckingham1">[16]</xref>
###xml 168 172 168 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Srivastava1">[17]</xref>
###xml 240 246 240 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Islet1</italic>
###xml 248 252 248 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Isl1</italic>
###xml 345 349 345 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Cai1">[18]</xref>
###xml 468 472 468 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Ai1">[19]</xref>
###xml 473 477 473 477 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Kwon1">[22]</xref>
###xml 586 590 583 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Isl1</italic>
###xml 602 606 599 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Lin1">[23]</xref>
###xml 838 842 835 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Hutson1">[24]</xref>
In the heart, normal development of the cardiac outflow tract requires the addition of cells from the secondary heart field (SHF) dorsal to the primary heart tube [16],[17]. SHF cells, which express the LIM-homeodomain transcription factor Islet1 (Isl1), migrate from the pharyngeal mesoderm to contribute to the myocardium of the outflow tract [18]. Recently canonical Wnt signaling has been shown to play a major role in the proliferation and expansion of SHF cells [19]-[22]. It has further been demonstrated that the canonical Wnt signaling mediator beta-catenin directly activates Isl1 expression [23]. Extensive remodeling of the outflow tract region with the addition of cardiac neural crest (CNC), mesenchyme from the crest of the neural folds, is then required to septate the single vessel to form the aorta and pulmonary artery [24]. Connections must form between the left ventricle and the aorta, as well as the right ventricle and pulmonary artery, to successfully establish both systemic and pulmonary circulation. Defects in the development of the outflow tract region cause phenotypes such as double outlet right ventricle (DORV), where both the pulmonary artery and the aorta connect to the right ventricle, transposition of the great arteries (TGA) and persistent truncus arteriosis (PTA), where the outflow tract fails to divide into an aorta and pulmonary artery.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 11 28 11 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Looptail (LtapLp)</italic>
###xml 70 85 70 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Van Gogh-like 2</italic>
###xml 87 93 87 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2</italic>
###xml 95 105 95 105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">strabismus</italic>
###xml 107 110 107 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Kibar1">[4]</xref>
###xml 111 115 111 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Murdoch1">[25]</xref>
###xml 241 254 241 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp/LtapLp</italic>
###xml 317 321 317 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Henderson1">[26]</xref>
###xml 488 492 488 492 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Henderson2">[27]</xref>
###xml 493 497 493 497 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Phillips1">[28]</xref>
###xml 617 622 617 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wnt11</italic>
###xml 622 626 622 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Zhou1">[29]</xref>
###xml 631 636 631 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wnt5a</italic>
###xml 636 640 636 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Schleiffarth1">[30]</xref>
###xml 642 647 642 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wnt5a</italic>
###xml 743 745 743 745 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 29 33 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 578 582 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Studies of Looptail (LtapLp) mice, which carry a missense mutation in Van Gogh-like 2 (Vangl2, strabismus) [4],[25], a component of the PCP pathway, have also implicated non-canonical Wnt signaling mechanisms in mammalian heart development. LtapLp/LtapLp homozygous mutants display the outflow tract abnormality DORV [26]. Reports indicate that the PCP pathway, which is necessary for the polarized migration of myocardial cells to the outflow tract septum, is disrupted in these mutants [27],[28]. Similar outflow tract defects including TGA and PTA have also been observed in mice lacking the non-canonical signals Wnt11[29] and Wnt5a[30]. Wnt5a has been proposed to function in the outflow tract by stimulating intracellular increases in Ca2+ to regulate cells of the CNC.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 108 111 108 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Curtin1">[3]</xref>
###xml 112 115 112 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Montcouquiol1">[5]</xref>
###xml 116 119 116 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang1">[6]</xref>
###xml 120 124 120 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Lu1">[31]</xref>
###xml 355 359 355 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Jones1">[32]</xref>
###xml 596 607 596 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2/Ltap</italic>
###xml 607 610 607 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Montcouquiol1">[5]</xref>
###xml 612 614 612 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fz</italic>
###xml 620 623 620 623 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fz6</italic>
###xml 623 627 623 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Guo1">[33]</xref>
###xml 628 632 628 632 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang2">[34]</xref>
###xml 637 641 637 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 646 650 646 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 650 653 650 653 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang1">[6]</xref>
###xml 790 794 790 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Jones1">[32]</xref>
###xml 914 917 914 917 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang1">[6]</xref>
###xml 918 922 918 922 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Chen1">[35]</xref>
###xml 549 554 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
PCP signaling is also required for the normal development of the auditory sensory organ, the organ of Corti [3],[5],[6],[31]. This structure is comprised of one row of inner and three rows of outer sensory hair cells, interdigitated with supporting cells such as inner phalangeal cells, the inner and outer pillar cells and the Deiters cells (reviewed in [32]). The sensory hair cells have stereociliary bundles uniformly orientated on the apical surfaces, which is the most obvious example of planar cell polarity in mammals. Consistent with this, mouse mutants of core PCP components including Vangl2/Ltap[5], Fz3 and Fz6[33],[34] and Dvl1 and Dvl2[6] display stereocilia misorientation, indicating that the correct alignment of these stereocilia is dependent on functional PCP signaling [32]. Cellular rearrangements characteristic of CE movements are also required during the development of the organ of Corti [6],[35], during which a thicker and shorter postmitotic primordium undergoes integrated cellular intercalation movements to produce extension along the longitudinal axis and narrowing along a perpendicular axis. Therefore signaling via the PCP pathway is responsible for both the polarized extension and the establishment of planar cell polarity in the organ of Corti.
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 249 253 249 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Ciruna1">[36]</xref>
###xml 254 258 254 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-YbotGonzalez1">[39]</xref>
###xml 363 374 363 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2/Ltap</italic>
###xml 374 377 374 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Kibar1">[4]</xref>
###xml 378 382 378 382 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Murdoch1">[25]</xref>
###xml 384 388 384 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 393 397 393 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 397 400 397 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang1">[6]</xref>
###xml 401 405 401 405 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Hamblet1">[40]</xref>
###xml 407 412 407 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Celsr</italic>
###xml 427 435 427 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">flamingo</italic>
###xml 437 440 437 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Curtin1">[3]</xref>
###xml 445 447 445 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fz</italic>
###xml 453 456 453 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Fz6</italic>
###xml 456 460 456 460 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang2">[34]</xref>
###xml 311 315 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The neural plate undergoes narrowing and lengthening attributable to CE movements during mammalian neurulation. When PCP signaling is disrupted, cells of the neuroepithelium fail to intercalate, preventing the neural tube from fusing at the midline [36]-[39]. Severe neural tube closure defects are observed in mice carrying mutations in PCP components including Vangl2/Ltap[4],[25], Dvl1 and Dvl2[6],[40], Celsr (a homolog of flamingo) [3] and Fz3 and Fz6[34]. These mutants have shorter and wider neural plates and display craniorachischisis, a completely open neural tube from mid-brain to tail.
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 34 38 34 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvls</italic>
###xml 115 118 115 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 227 231 227 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 350 354 350 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Lijam2">[41]</xref>
###xml 489 493 489 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 508 512 508 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Hamblet1">[40]</xref>
###xml 555 558 555 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 723 727 723 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 727 730 727 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 731 735 731 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 735 738 735 738 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 896 899 896 899 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 910 914 910 914 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Wang3">[38]</xref>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Hamblet1">[40]</xref>
###xml 83 88 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 241 245 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 503 507 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
To elucidate the role of specific Dvls in mammalian development, we have generated mouse knockouts for each of the Dvl genes. Interestingly distinct phenotypes were revealed, suggesting separate functions for the Dvl proteins. Dvl1 knockout mice are viable and fertile, but display social interaction abnormalities and defects in sensorimotor gating [41]. By contrast, incompletely penetrant cardiac outflow tract abnormalities (50%) and rib/vertebral malformations (>90%) are observed in Dvl2 knockout mice [40]. However, functional redundancy among the Dvl genes is also suggested from their overlapping expression patterns, as well as their high degree of conservation. In support of this, we have previously shown that Dvl1-/-;Dvl2-/- mutants display craniorachischisis, a completely open neural tube, and abnormalities in the organ of Corti, both novel phenotypes not observed in the single Dvl knockouts [38],[40].
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 345 349 345 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 369 373 369 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 378 382 378 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 439 443 439 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 602 605 602 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl</italic>
###xml 34 38 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Here we describe the phenotype of mice deficient in Dvl3 and determine its importance in conotruncal, cochlear and neural tube development. Given the overlapping expression patterns of the Dvls, as well as their high degree of conservation, we further addressed the possibility of functional redundancy and demonstrate that many of the roles of Dvl3 are also shared by Dvl1 and Dvl2. We attribute several of the developmental functions of Dvl3 to its role in PCP signaling, enhancing our knowledge of this essential pathway in mammalian development and further defining the specific role of individual Dvl genes.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
Results
###end title 17
###begin title 18
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 23 26 23 26 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Cardiac Defects in Dvl3-/- Mutants
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 49 58 49 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000259.s001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 112 116 112 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 116 119 116 119 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 153 157 153 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 209 218 209 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 278 282 278 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 282 285 282 285 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 318 322 318 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 322 325 322 325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 330 334 330 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 334 337 334 337 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 535 539 535 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 539 542 539 542 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 588 592 588 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 592 595 592 595 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 597 601 597 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 601 604 601 604 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 609 613 609 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 613 616 613 616 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 729 733 729 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 906 910 906 910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 910 913 910 913 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 15 19 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 120 124 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 543 547 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 914 918 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Dvl3 knock out mice were successfully generated (Figure S1). In order to calculate the frequency of survival of Dvl3-/- mice, the genotypes of pups from Dvl3 heterozygote crosses were analyzed at weaning age (Figure 1A). In a 129S6 inbred background, 97 pups were genotyped. No Dvl3-/- pups survived to weaning, while Dvl3+/+ and Dvl3+/- pups were observed in an approximate 1:2 ratio (34 and 63 respectively), as expected from Mendelian ratios. In a mixed genetic background, 121 pups were analyzed, but only 4 out of the expected 30 Dvl3-/- mice (13.3%) survived. In contrast, at E18.5 Dvl3+/+, Dvl3+/- and Dvl3-/- genotypes were recovered in normal Mendelian ratios from heterozygous crosses. These data indicate that 100% of Dvl3 homozygotes in a 129S6 inbred background and approximately 87% in a mixed genetic background die shortly after birth. No gross abnormalities were observed in the few adult Dvl3-/- mice that did survive in a mixed background.
###end p 19
###begin title 20
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 33 37 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Cardiac defects of Dvl3 knockout mice.
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 39 43 39 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 186 190 186 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 190 193 190 193 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 247 251 247 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 251 254 251 254 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 424 428 424 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 428 431 428 431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 443 447 443 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 447 450 447 450 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 721 730 717 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3-EYFP</italic>
###xml 787 791 783 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 791 794 787 790 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 194 198 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
The genotypes of weaning age pups from Dvl3 heterozygote crosses, in both an inbred 129S6 and mixed genetic background, were collected in order to calculate the frequency of survival of Dvl3-/- mice (A). Cardiac abnormalities were observed in all Dvl3-/- mutants examined in an inbred background (B-D). Whole mounts (B), scanning electron microscopy images (C) and hematoxylin and eosin stained sections (D) of P0 hearts of Dvl3+/+ (left) and Dvl3-/- hearts that displayed PTA (middle) and DORV (right). Aorta (Ao), pulmonary artery (PA), right ventricle (RV), left ventricle (LV). Deconvolution microscopy image showing EYFP-Dvl3 BAC transgene expression in the heart at E9.5. White bar = 20 microm (E). Addition of the Dvl3-EYFP transgene (G) rescues the abnormal cardiac phenotype of Dvl3-/- mutants (F, heart displays PTA).
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 4 7 4 7 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 98 102 98 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 102 105 102 105 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 121 130 121 130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 168 177 168 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1C</xref>
###xml 207 216 207 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1D</xref>
Dvl3-/- newborn pups had difficulty breathing and were often cyanotic. Examination of hearts from Dvl3-/- mutants at P0 (Figure 1B) using scanning electron microscopy (Figure 1C) and histochemical analysis (Figure 1D) revealed that all had conotruncal abnormalities. More specifically, seven of the eleven mutant hearts displayed PTA, the outflow tract having failed to divide into an aorta and pulmonary artery, and four showed DORV, where both the pulmonary artery and the aorta connected to the right ventricle.
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 83 92 83 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen.1000259.s002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 194 203 194 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1E</xref>
###xml 256 260 256 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 260 263 260 263 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 322 326 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 326 329 326 329 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 373 377 373 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 402 406 402 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 406 409 406 409 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 427 431 427 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 448 452 448 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 547 551 547 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 551 554 551 554 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 609 613 609 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 613 616 613 616 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 685 689 685 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 689 692 689 692 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 710 714 710 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 785 801 785 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g001">Figure 1F and 1G</xref>
We generated an EYFP-tagged Dvl3 transgene using homologous recombination of BACs (Figure S2) and observed expression of Dvl3-EYFP in the embryonic heart during conotruncal development at E9.5 (Figure 1E). This transgene fully rescued the lethal defect in Dvl3-/- mutants, providing formal proof that the phenotype of the Dvl3-/- mutants is specifically due to the loss of Dvl3. From a cross between a Dvl3-/- rescued with the Dvl3 transgene and a Dvl3 heterozygote (both in a mixed background), 31% (37/118) of pups genotyped at weaning age were Dvl3-/- rescued with the transgene, whereas only 1.6% (2/118) Dvl3-/- mutants survived without the transgene. E18.5 hearts collected from Dvl3-/- embryos with the Dvl3 transgene appeared normal and displayed no conotruncal abnormalities (Figure 1F and 1G).
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 27 30 27 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 31 35 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Conotruncal Defects in Dvl3-/- Mice Are Not Due to an Absence of CNC or SHF Cells
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 149 153 149 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 153 156 153 156 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 304 320 304 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Rosa-26-lacZ Cre</italic>
###xml 397 405 394 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wnt1-Cre</italic>
###xml 483 494 480 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g002">Figure 2A&#8211;H</xref>
###xml 542 550 539 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Isl1-Cre</italic>
###xml 552 563 549 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g002">Figure 2I&#8211;P</xref>
###xml 699 703 696 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 703 706 700 703 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Normal development of the outflow tract requires contribution from both the CNC and SHF, so we examined whether a lack of either of these tissues in Dvl3-/- mutants may be responsible for the observed conotruncal defects by lineage tracing experiments using lineage-specific Cre/LoxP recombination and a Rosa-26-lacZ Cre reporter that expresses beta-galactosidase only in cells with Cre activity. Wnt1-Cre, expressed in neural crest cells, was used to label the CNC cell population (Figure 2A-H) and SHF cells were specifically labeled using Isl1-Cre (Figure 2I-P). Embryos were collected and stained at E10.5, E14.5 and E18.5. At each of these stages both CNC and SHF cells were clearly evident in Dvl3-/- mutants, suggesting that the outflow tract defects were not due to an appreciable loss of either of these lineages.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 56 60 56 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 60 63 60 63 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Cells of both the CNC and SHF lineage remain present in Dvl3-/- mutants.
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 206 210 203 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 210 213 207 210 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 223 230 220 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wnt1Cre</italic>
###xml 300 307 297 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Isl1Cre</italic>
###xml 367 371 364 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 371 374 368 371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/+</sup>
###xml 397 401 394 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 401 404 398 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
Lineage tracing experiments using lineage-specific Cre/LoxP recombination and a Rosa-26-lacZ Cre reporter that drives expression of beta-galactosidase were performed to identify cells of the CNC and SHF in Dvl3-/- mutants. Wnt1Cre was used to specifically label cells from the neural crest (A-H) and Isl1Cre to label the SHF (I-P) at various stages of development in Dvl3+/+ (A,C,E,G,I,K,M,O) and Dvl3-/- mutants (B,D,F,H,J,L,N,P). At E10.5 whole embryos (A,B,I,J) were dissected to visualize the conotruncus (C,D,K,L, arrows). At E14.5 (E,F,M,N) and E18.5 (G,H,O,P) hearts were sectioned to examine staining. Aorta (Ao), pulmonary artery (PA), persistent truncus arteriosis (PTA).
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 28 34 28 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 42 46 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Neural Tube Defects in Dvl3;LtapLp Mutant Mice
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 41 44 41 44 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 80 84 80 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 84 87 84 87 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 88 89 88 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</italic>
###xml 89 92 89 92 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 144 148 144 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Hamblet1">[40]</xref>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 320 329 320 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EYFP-Dvl3</italic>
###xml 368 377 368 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ECFP-Dvl1</italic>
###xml 407 411 407 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl1</italic>
###xml 411 414 411 414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 415 419 415 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl2</italic>
###xml 419 422 419 422 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 543 554 543 554 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3A&#8211;C</xref>
###xml 291 306 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">transgenic mice</span>
Neural tube defects were observed in Dvl2-/- mutants and to a greater extent in Dvl1-/-;2-/- double knockouts, indicating functional redundancy [40]. We examined a potential role for Dvl3 in neural tube closure. To determine expression of Dvl3 and Dvl1 in the developing neural tube we used transgenic mice carrying the EYFP-Dvl3 transgene and another, similarly made ECFP-Dvl1 transgene, which rescues the Dvl1-/-;Dvl2-/- lethal phenotype (data not shown). Expression of both Dvl3 and Dvl1 was observed in the developing neural tube at E9.5 (Figure 3A-C), an important time for this developmental process. The colors were artificially changed to red and green for Dvl3 and Dvl1, respectively, for easy observation of colocalization (yellow). These Dvls appeared to colocalize in many cells (indicated with white arrows), but not in all cells.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 23 34 23 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3/LtapLp</italic>
Neural tube defects in Dvl3/LtapLp mutants.
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 270 274 270 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 274 277 274 277 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 278 284 278 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 433 437 433 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 437 440 437 440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 441 447 441 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 601 605 601 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 605 608 605 608 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 609 615 609 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 668 672 668 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 672 675 672 675 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 676 682 676 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
Expression of Dvl1-ECFP transgene (green) and Dvl3-EYFP transgene (red) in the developing neural tube at E9.5 (A,B, both individual z-plane confocal images and C, a rotated z-stacked image). Colocalization of these Dvls was evident in many cells (white arrows). Several Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ embryos collected at E18.5 appeared normal (D-F), but others displayed neural tube defects such as exencephaly or craniorachischisis (H-J). E18.5 Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ embryos also showed both normal (L-N) and defective (P-R) neurulation. The hearts of these mutants were also examined (G,K,O,S) and appeared normal in Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ embryos but conotruncal defects were displayed in Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 11 17 11 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 18 24 18 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 72 83 72 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2/Ltap</italic>
###xml 166 169 166 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Kibar1">[4]</xref>
###xml 170 174 170 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen.1000259-Murdoch1">[25]</xref>
###xml 223 229 223 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 307 311 307 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 311 314 311 314 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 409 413 409 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 427 433 427 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 450 454 450 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 454 457 454 457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 458 464 458 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 517 528 517 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3D&#8211;F</xref>
###xml 610 621 610 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3H&#8211;J</xref>
###xml 722 726 722 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 726 729 726 729 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 730 736 730 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 776 787 776 787 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3L&#8211;N</xref>
###xml 831 842 831 842 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3P&#8211;R</xref>
###xml 896 900 896 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 900 903 900 903 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 904 910 904 910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 979 983 979 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 983 986 983 986 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 987 993 987 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 1168 1172 1168 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1172 1175 1172 1175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1176 1182 1176 1182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 1205 1209 1205 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 1209 1212 1209 1212 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1213 1219 1213 1219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 436 440 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Homozygous LtapLp;LtapLp mutants of the PCP signaling pathway component Vangl2/Ltap, display craniorachischisis, a completely open neural tube from mid-brain to tail [4],[25], whereas no neural tube defects are observed in LtapLp/+ heterozygotes. Although no neural tube defects were observed in any of the Dvl3-/- mutant embryos collected (data not shown), defective neurulation was apparent when we crossed Dvl3 mutants with LtapLp/+ mice. Several Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ embryos displayed normal neural tube development (Figure 3D-F), whereas others exhibited neural tube abnormalities such as craniorachischisis (Figure 3H-J) and exencephaly, defective closure of the rostral neural tube. Similar phenotypes were observed in Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants, with some appearing normal (Figure 3L-N) and others displaying craniorachischisis (Figure 3P-R). The frequency of these defects was similar in both Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ (7/22, 32%, 5 with craniorachischisis and 2 with exencephaly) and Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants (6/16, 38%, all with craniorachischisis). However, craniorachischisis appears to be a more severe phenotype than exencephaly, indicating a more severe phenotype in Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants compared to Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ mutants.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 8 12 8 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 12 15 12 15 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 20 26 20 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 27 33 27 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 146 150 146 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 150 153 150 153 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 154 160 154 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 185 201 185 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3G and 3K</xref>
###xml 309 313 309 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 313 316 313 316 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 317 323 317 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 346 362 346 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g003">Figure 3O and 3S</xref>
###xml 411 415 411 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 415 418 415 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 340 344 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 418 422 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
As both Dvl3-/- and LtapLp;LtapLp mutants display cardiac defects but the single heterozygotes do not, we looked for defects in the hearts of the Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ double heterozygotes (Figure 3G and 3K). However, all hearts appeared normal, even in the mutants with neural tube defects, while all hearts from Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ double mutant mice (Figure 3O and 3S) displayed conotruncal defects, as expected for Dvl3-/-mice.
###end p 33
###begin title 34
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 23 26 23 26 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 27 31 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mice</span>
Cochlea Defects in Dvl3-/- Mice
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 200 211 200 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vangl2/Ltap</italic>
###xml 213 219 213 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>

###xml 2089 2098 2089 2098 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g004">Figure 4L</xref>
###xml 2169 2173 2169 2173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 2173 2176 2173 2176 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2177 2183 2177 2183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 2190 2194 2190 2194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Dvl3</italic>
###xml 2194 2197 2194 2197 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2198 2204 2198 2204 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LtapLp</italic>
###xml 2351 2360 2351 2360 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-1000259-g004">Figure 4K</xref>
###xml 129 134 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
A major role for the mammalian PCP pathway in the development of the organ of Corti has previously been described. Cochleae from mouse mutants homozygous for a mutant allele of the core PCP component Vangl2/Ltap (LtapLp;LtapLp), display misorientation of stereociliary bundles in sensory hair cells due to disrupted planar cell polarity and the cochlear ducts are also shortened and wider due to defects in CE cell movements [5],[6]. We have shown that both Dvl1 and Dvl2 function in PCP signaling in the developing cochlea [6]. To assess whether Dvl3 also functions in this process, we examined cochleae from Dvl3 mutant embryos, with and without an extra LtapLp mutation in Vangl2. No cochlear defects were observed in either Dvl3+/- (data not shown) or LtapLp/+ single heterozygotes in the basal and middle regions (Figs 4A and 4E). However, a mild PCP phenotype was observed in Dvl3-/- cochleae, where the uniform orientation of stereociliary bundles was disrupted in some hair cells in both the base and the middle of the cochlear ducts (Figure 4B and 4F, respectively). The cochleae of Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ mutants that had normal neural tube development were unaffected. However, in the Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ mutants that showed defective neurulation, a PCP phenotype in the cochlea accompanied the neural tube defect, with the misorientation of several sensory hair cells in both the basal and middle regions (Figure 4C and 4G, respectively). Compared to these two mutants the severity of the phenotype was much increased in Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants that showed neural tube defects, in which many hair cells had disrupted orientation (Figure 4D and 4H). Misorientation of stereociliary bundles was also observed in Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants that had normal neural tube development, but the phenotype was much weaker than in embryos of the same genotype displaying defective neurulation. In the apical regions of the cochlear ducts, rotated stereociliary bundles were observed in the hair cells of LtapLp/+ (Figure 4I), Dvl3-/- (Figure 4J), Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ (Figure 4K) and Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ (Figure 4L) mutants, although the number of cells affected was increased in both Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ and Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ mutants. In these combined mutants the degree of rotation also appeared more severe, as several stereociliary bundles were completely reversed (Figure 4K).
###end p 35

(A-L) Confocal images (100x) of the surface of cochlear whole mounts isolated at E18.5 from LtapLp/+ (A,E,I), Dvl3-/- (B, F,J), Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ (C,G,K), Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ (D,H,L). Images show comparable regions in each mouse at the base (A-D), middle (E-H) and apex (I-L) of the cochlear ducts. In A-L brackets and arrowheads indicate the outer and inner hair cells, respectively. In A-H white stars indicate misoriented stereociliary bundles and in I-L dotted circles in the left panels outline regions presented in the right panels. (M-P) Light micrographs of the inner ears (top) and isolated cochlea ducts (bottom) isolated at E18.5 from LtapLp/+ (M), Dvl3-/- (N), Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ (O), Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ (P) samples. The yellow dotted line traces each cochlear spiral and the brackets indicate the cochlea portion of the inner ear. (Q-S) Confocal images (40x) of the surface of cochlear whole mounts isolated at E18.5 from LtapLp/+ (Q), Dvl3+/-;LtapLp/+ (R), Dvl3-/-;LtapLp/+ (S) mutants. Images show comparable regions in each cochlea. (T) Expression of Dvl3-EYFP transgene (green) and stereocilary bundles (red) in the vestibular utricle region of the inner ear. White stars indicate cells in which the asymmetric localization of Dvl3 is very clear. (U) Expression of Dvl3-EYFP transgene in the cochlear duct. Arrows indicate the polarized localization of Dvl3, towards the lateral side of the sensory hair cells.
